| Interview with Prajit Datta, AI Research Scientist, AFRY<br/><br/>How his team used AI to develop a social distancing tool to be used during times of pandemic.<br/><br/>His advices to beginners in data science who are starting out their careers.<br/><br/>How did you first get into data science?<br/><br/>Right from the university days, I had an inclination towards strategy making which was used to run my own student chapter. I always get fascinated by seeing how data reveals a lot of details and helps you build strategies around that. Those collective moments got me to explore the field of data science and learn new technologies around that. I started learning R and did some basic analytical projects and that's how it all started.<br/><br/>How is data science used to create value in your current project(s)?<br/><br/>In my current projects, We deal mostly with neural networks and image processing. It always gives us insights and interesting predictions. For example, in this the current pandemic situation, We have developed an AI Social Distancing Tool called Flowity which can be utilized by governments and organization to monitor and control the crowd. It can detect if people are keeping a safe distance from each other by analyzing real-time video streams from the camera in a GDPR safe way!<br/><br/>What are the key skills that you use every day as a data scientist, and how did you develop them?<br/><br/>To become a good data scientist, you need to have a mix of three major skillsets : Business domain knowledge, Statistics, and Programming.<br/><br/>Domain knowledge increases with your day to day experiences.<br/><br/>AI Time Journal Resources<br/><br/>Are you learning data science?<br/><br/>Check out what books helped 20+ successful data scientists grow in their career.<br/><br/>For learning statistics, you need to read some standard books, pursue online courses, and read research papers.<br/><br/>And Programming, It's all about the practice and getting myself updated with modern packages and tools.<br/><br/>What are the top challenges you currently face as a professional data scientist, and how do you go about tackling them?<br/><br/>I think the biggest challenge for any professional data scientist is to handle large unstructured datasets especially at the stages of data collection and pre-processing â€“ cleaning, profiling, and quality. The tackling strategies depend on the problem statements as well as datasets. There is no fixed strategy around that. The better the data, the more we are likely to get better resultsDo you create data science content?<br/><br/>Yes, I am in process of launching my own data science online course this year and post that, will be also releasing my next book on that. It will be for business leaders and project managers.<br/><br/>3 words that best summarize how you learned ML and data science:<br/><br/>Explore, Practice & Experience!<br/><br/>People: who are some inspiring data scientists and people in AI that you follow?<br/><br/>I follow the works of many but my idols are Andrew Ng, Yann LeCun and Geoffrey Hinton.<br/><br/>Books: which books have helped you the most in your journey and why?<br/><br/>Courses: what courses/programs have you taken that have significantly contributed to advancing your career in data science?<br/><br/>I would like to recommend a few fundamental courses listed in Coursera by Andrew Ng, Regular participation in Data Science Challenges hosted at Kaggle and other forums can help anyone to advance their career in data science and be updated with new techniques.<br/><br/>What advice would you give to someone who wants to get into data science today?<br/><br/>Even though there are modern tools and platforms to make our work easy, never ever skip learning the fundamentals. This is the base on which we build data science projects.<br/><br/>Also, always work on your business domain knowledge, which you mostly will get outside the data science circles.<br/><br/>What inspires you about working in Data Science?<br/><br/>I really like the multi-disciplinary approach involved in data science, where we learn every day and find happiness in solving real-life problems and build strategies to mitigate risk and make this world a better place. | Î£Ï…Î½Î­Î½Ï„ÎµÏ…Î¾Î· Î¼Îµ Ï„Î¿Î½ Prajit Datta, AI Research Scientist, AFRY<br/><br/>Î ÏÏ‚ Î· Î¿Î¼Î¬Î´Î± Ï„Î¿Ï… Ï‡ÏÎ·ÏƒÎ¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î·ÏƒÎµ Ï„Î¿ AI Î³Î¹Î± Î½Î± Î±Î½Î±Ï€Ï„ÏÎ¾ÎµÎ¹ Î­Î½Î± ÎºÎ¿Î¹Î½Ï‰Î½Î¹ÎºÏŒ ÎµÏÎ³Î±Î»ÎµÎ¯Î¿ Î±Ï€Î¿ÏƒÏ„Î±ÏƒÎ¹Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î·ÏƒÎ·Ï‚ Î³Î¹Î± Î½Î± Ï‡ÏÎ·ÏƒÎ¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¹Î·Î¸ÎµÎ¯ ÏƒÎµ Ï€ÎµÏÎ¹ÏŒÎ´Î¿Ï…Ï‚ Ï€Î±Î½Î´Î·Î¼Î¯Î±Ï‚.<br/><br/>ÎŸÎ¹ ÏƒÏ…Î¼Î²Î¿Ï…Î»Î­Ï‚ Ï„Î¿Ï… ÏƒÎµ Î±ÏÏ‡Î¬ÏÎ¹Î¿Ï…Ï‚ ÏƒÏ„Î·Î½ ÎµÏ€Î¹ÏƒÏ„Î®Î¼Î· Ï„Ï‰Î½ Î´ÎµÎ´Î¿Î¼Î­Î½Ï‰Î½ Ï€Î¿Ï… Î¾ÎµÎºÎ¹Î½Î¿ÏÎ½ Ï„Î·Î½ ÎºÎ±ÏÎ¹Î­ÏÎ± Ï„Î¿Ï…Ï‚.<br/><br/>Î ÏÏ‚ Î¼Ï€Î®ÎºÎµÏ‚ Î³Î¹Î± Ï€ÏÏÏ„Î· Ï†Î¿ÏÎ¬ ÏƒÏ„Î·Î½ ÎµÏ€Î¹ÏƒÏ„Î®Î¼Î· Ï„Ï‰Î½ Î´ÎµÎ´Î¿Î¼Î­Î½Ï‰Î½;<br/><br/>Î‘Ï€ÏŒ Ï„Î¹Ï‚ Î¼Î­ÏÎµÏ‚ Ï„Î¿Ï… Ï€Î±Î½ÎµÏ€Î¹ÏƒÏ„Î·Î¼Î¯Î¿Ï…, ÎµÎ¯Ï‡Î± Î¼Î¹Î± ÎºÎ»Î¯ÏƒÎ· Ï€ÏÎ¿Ï‚ Ï„Î· Ï‡Î¬ÏÎ±Î¾Î· ÏƒÏ„ÏÎ±Ï„Î·Î³Î¹ÎºÎ®Ï‚ Î· Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î± Ï‡ÏÎ·ÏƒÎ¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¹Î®Î¸Î·ÎºÎµ Î³Î¹Î± Î½Î± Ï„ÏÎ­Î¾ÎµÎ¹ Ï„Î¿ Î´Î¹ÎºÏŒ Î¼Î¿Ï… Ï†Î¿Î¹Ï„Î·Ï„Î¹ÎºÏŒ ÎºÎµÏ†Î¬Î»Î±Î¹Î¿. Î‘Ï…Ï„Î® ÎµÎ¯Î½Î±Î¹ Î· Î²Î¬ÏƒÎ· Ï€Î¬Î½Ï‰ ÏƒÏ„Î·Î½ Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î± Ï‡Ï„Î¯Î¶Î¿Ï…Î¼Îµ Î­ÏÎ³Î± ÎµÏ€Î¹ÏƒÏ„Î®Î¼Î·Ï‚ Î´ÎµÎ´Î¿Î¼Î­Î½Ï‰Î½.<br/><br/>Î•Ï€Î¯ÏƒÎ·Ï‚, Ï€Î¬Î½Ï„Î± Î½Î± ÎµÏÎ³Î¬Î¶ÎµÏƒÏ„Îµ ÏƒÏ„Î· Î³Î½ÏÏƒÎ· Ï„Î¿Ï… Ï„Î¿Î¼Î­Î± Ï„Î·Ï‚ ÎµÏ€Î¹Ï‡ÎµÎ¯ÏÎ·ÏƒÎ®Ï‚ ÏƒÎ±Ï‚, Ï„Î·Î½ Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î± Ï‰Ï‚ ÎµÏ€Î¯ Ï„Î¿ Ï€Î»ÎµÎ¯ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î½ Î¸Î± Ï€Î¬ÏÎµÏ„Îµ Î­Î¾Ï‰ Î±Ï€ÏŒ Ï„Î¿Ï…Ï‚ ÎºÏÎºÎ»Î¿Ï…Ï‚ Ï„Î·Ï‚ ÎµÏ€Î¹ÏƒÏ„Î®Î¼Î·Ï‚ Ï„Ï‰Î½ Î´ÎµÎ´Î¿Î¼Î­Î½Ï‰Î½.<br/><br/>Î¤Î¹ ÏƒÎ±Ï‚ ÎµÎ¼Ï€Î½Î­ÎµÎ¹ ÏƒÏ‡ÎµÏ„Î¹ÎºÎ¬ Î¼Îµ Ï„Î·Î½ ÎµÏÎ³Î±ÏƒÎ¯Î± ÏƒÏ„Î·Î½ Î•Ï€Î¹ÏƒÏ„Î®Î¼Î· Ï„Ï‰Î½ Î”ÎµÎ´Î¿Î¼Î­Î½Ï‰Î½;<br/><br/>ÎœÎ¿Ï… Î±ÏÎ­ÏƒÎµÎ¹ Ï€ÏÎ±Î³Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÎ¬ Î· Î´Î¹ÎµÏ€Î¹ÏƒÏ„Î·Î¼Î¿Î½Î¹ÎºÎ® Ï€ÏÎ¿ÏƒÎ­Î³Î³Î¹ÏƒÎ· Ï€Î¿Ï… ÎµÎ¼Ï€Î»Î­ÎºÎµÏ„Î±Î¹ ÏƒÏ„Î·Î½ ÎµÏ€Î¹ÏƒÏ„Î®Î¼Î· Ï„Ï‰Î½ Î´ÎµÎ´Î¿Î¼Î­Î½Ï‰Î½, ÏŒÏ€Î¿Ï… Î¼Î±Î¸Î±Î¯Î½Î¿Ï…Î¼Îµ ÎºÎ¬Î¸Îµ Î¼Î­ÏÎ± ÎºÎ±Î¹ Î²ÏÎ¯ÏƒÎºÎ¿Ï…Î¼Îµ ÎµÏ…Ï„Ï…Ï‡Î¯Î± ÏƒÏ„Î·Î½ ÎµÏ€Î¯Î»Ï…ÏƒÎ· Ï€ÏÎ¿Î²Î»Î·Î¼Î¬Ï„Ï‰Î½ Ï„Î·Ï‚ Ï€ÏÎ±Î³Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÎ®Ï‚ Î¶Ï‰Î®Ï‚ ÎºÎ±Î¹ ÎºÎ±Ï„Î±ÏƒÎºÎµÏ…Î¬Î¶Î¿Ï…Î¼Îµ ÏƒÏ„ÏÎ±Ï„Î·Î³Î¹ÎºÎ­Ï‚ Î³Î¹Î± Î½Î± Î¼ÎµÏ„ÏÎ¹Î¬ÏƒÎ¿Ï…Î¼Îµ Ï„Î¿Î½ ÎºÎ¯Î½Î´Ï…Î½Î¿ ÎºÎ±Î¹ Î½Î± ÎºÎ¬Î½Î¿Ï…Î¼Îµ Î±Ï…Ï„ÏŒÎ½ Ï„Î¿Î½ ÎºÏŒÏƒÎ¼Î¿ Î­Î½Î± ÎºÎ±Î»ÏÏ„ÎµÏÎ¿ Î¼Î­ÏÎ¿Ï‚. |
| Linux and UNIX Man Pages<br/><br/>Linux & Unix Commands - Search Man Pages<br/><br/>stack(5) [bsd man page]<br/><br/>STACK(5) File Formats Manual STACK(5)NAME<br/>stack - 2.10BSD PDP-11 C stack frame conventions<br/>DESCRIPTION<br/>The standard C stack frame layout:<br/>------------------<br/>&#124;...nth argument &#124; push arguments in reverse order<br/>------------------<br/>&#124;second argument &#124;<br/>------------------<br/>&#124; first argument &#124;<br/>------------------ JSR PC,*$_FOO<br/>&#124; return address &#124;<br/>------------------ JSR R5,CSV<br/>&#124; old R5 value &#124; <-----<br/>------------------ &#124;<br/>&#124;previous overlay&#124; &#124;<br/>&#124; number &#124; &#124;<br/>------------------ &#124;<br/>&#124; r4 &#124; &#124;<br/>------------------ &#124;<br/>&#124; r3 &#124; &#124;<br/>------------------ &#124;<br/>&#124; r2 &#124; &#124;<br/>------------------ &#124;<br/>&#124; first local var&#124; &#124; This is the top of the stack<br/>------------------ &#124; when the called routine ''starts''<br/>&#124; routine &#124; &#124;<br/>&#124; allocates &#124; &#124;<br/>&#124; storage &#124; &#124; SUB $n,SP<br/>&#124; temporary &#124; &#124;<br/>------------------ &#124;<br/>&#124; push arguments &#124; &#124;<br/>&#124; of next routine&#124; &#124;<br/>------------------ &#124; JSR PC,*$_BAR<br/>&#124; return address &#124; &#124;<br/>------------------ &#124; JSR R5,CSV<br/>&#124; old R5 value---+-------<br/>------------------ ^<br/>&#124;previous overlay&#124; &#124;<br/>&#124; number &#124; &#124;<br/>------------------ &#124;<br/>&#124; r4/43/r2/... &#124; &#124;<br/>------------------<br/>&#124; and so on..... &#124;<br/>The stack pushes downward through memory addresses. Overlay numbers saved in non-overlaid objects are always zero, but the simplification<br/>of not having to maintain two different stack frame formats more than outweighs the extra few micro seconds (less than four) necessary to<br/>save the zero ...<br/>Functions returning integers leave their return value in R0; functions returning floating constants use FR0; functions returning longs<br/>leave return values in R1/R0 (R0 high word, R1 low); functions returning structures leave a pointer to bss storage (one chunk of which is<br/>allocated for each such routine) in R0, and the caller will copy from that bss storage to the local destination.<br/>Local variables are allocated in such a way that they are referred to as ''-N(R5)'', arguments are referred to as ''+N(R5)''; arguments<br/>start at 4(R5), the first integer local declared will be at -10(R5).<br/>The SP normally points at the first word available for parameter pushing. A function taking only single word as a parameter can be called<br/>simply by moving the parameter into (SP) and calling the function, without having to clean the parameter off the stack on return. Any<br/>parameters passed after the first (actually "Nth") must be pushed before the call and cleaned off afterwards. If the function has no local<br/>variables and calls no functions, it will allocate no stack and the word labelled ''first local var'' will be unused.<br/>It is important to note that routines know how many arguments they pass to a function, and will adjust the stack accordingly after a func-<br/>tion returns.<br/>NOTE<br/>This stack frame format is the same as that used by overlaid objects in 2.9BSD.<br/>AUTHOR<br/>John F. Woods, MIT Concouse Computer Center<br/>3rd Berkeley DistributionSTACK(5)<br/><br/>Check Out this Related Man Page<br/><br/>STACK(9) BSD Kernel Developer's Manual STACK(9)NAME<br/>stack -- kernel thread stack tracing routines<br/>SYNOPSIS<br/>#include <sys/param.h><br/>#include <sys/stack.h><br/>In the kernel configuration file:<br/>options DDB<br/>options STACK<br/>struct stack *<br/>stack_create(void);<br/>void<br/>stack_destroy(struct stack *st);<br/>int<br/>stack_put(struct stack *st, vm_offset_t pc);<br/>void<br/>stack_copy(struct stack *src, struct stack dst);<br/>void<br/>stack_zero(struct stack *st);<br/>void<br/>stack_print(struct stack *st);<br/>void<br/>stack_print_ddb(struct stack *st);<br/>void<br/>stack_print_short(struct stack *st);<br/>void<br/>stack_print_short_ddb(struct stack *st);<br/>void<br/>stack_sbuf_print(struct sbuf sb*, struct stack *st);<br/>void<br/>stack_sbuf_print_ddb(struct sbuf sb*, struct stack *st);<br/>void<br/>stack_save(struct stack *st);<br/>DESCRIPTION<br/>The stack KPI allows querying of kernel stack trace information and the automated generation of kernel stack trace strings for the purposes<br/>of debugging and tracing. To use the KPI, at least one of options DDB and options STACK must be compiled into the kernel.<br/>Each stack trace is described by a struct stack. Before a trace may be created or otherwise manipulated, storage for the trace must be allo-<br/>cated with stack_create(), which may sleep. Memory associated with a trace is freed by calling stack_destroy().<br/>A trace of the current kernel thread's call stack may be captured using stack_save().<br/>stack_print() and stack_print_short() may be used to print a stack trace using the kernel printf(9), and may sleep as a result of acquiring<br/>sx(9) locks in the kernel linker while looking up symbol names. In locking-sensitive environments, the unsynchronized stack_print_ddb() and<br/>stack_print_short_ddb() variants may be invoked. This function bypasses kernel linker locking, making it usable in ddb(4), but not in a live<br/>system where linker data structures may change.<br/>stack_sbuf_print() may be used to construct a human-readable string, including conversion (where possible) from a simple kernel instruction<br/>pointer to a named symbol and offset. The argument sb must be an initialized struct sbuf as described in sbuf(9). This function may sleep<br/>if an auto-extending struct sbuf is used, or due to kernel linker locking. In locking-sensitive environments, such as ddb(4), the unsynchro-<br/>nized stack_sbuf_print_ddb() variant may be invoked to avoid kernel linker locking; it should be used with a fixed-length sbuf.<br/>The utility functions stack_zero, stack_copy, and stack_put may be used to manipulate stack data structures directly.<br/>SEE ALSO ddb(4), printf(9), sbuf(9), sx(9)AUTHORS<br/>The stack(9) function suite was created by Antoine Brodin. stack(9) was extended by Robert Watson for general-purpose use outside of ddb(4).<br/>BSD June 24, 2009 BSD | Linux ÎºÎ±Î¹ UNIX Man Î£ÎµÎ»Î¯Î´ÎµÏ‚<br/><br/>Î•Î½Ï„Î¿Î»Î­Ï‚ Linux & Unix - Î‘Î½Î±Î¶Î®Ï„Î·ÏƒÎ· Man Pages<br/><br/>ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î±(5) [ÏƒÎµÎ»Î¯Î´Î± bsd man]<br/><br/>STACK(5) ÎœÎ¿ÏÏ†Î­Ï‚ Î±ÏÏ‡ÎµÎ¯Ï‰Î½ Î§ÎµÎ¹ÏÎ¿ÎºÎ¯Î½Î·Ï„Î· ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î± STACK(5)NAME - 2.10BSD PDP-11 C ÏƒÏ…Î¼Î²Î¬ÏƒÎµÎ¹Ï‚ Ï€Î»Î±Î¹ÏƒÎ¯Î¿Ï… ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î±Ï‚<br/>Î Î•Î¡Î™Î“Î¡Î‘Î¦Î—<br/>Î— Ï„Ï…Ï€Î¹ÎºÎ® Î´Î¹Î¬Ï„Î±Î¾Î· Ï€Î»Î±Î¹ÏƒÎ¯Î¿Ï… ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î±Ï‚ C:<br/>-------------------------------------------------------<br/>Î— Ï€Î±ÏÎ¬Î¼ÎµÏ„ÏÎ¿Ï‚ "...nth argument" ÏƒÏ€ÏÏÏ‡Î½ÎµÎ¹ Ï„Î± ÎµÏ€Î¹Ï‡ÎµÎ¹ÏÎ®Î¼Î±Ï„Î± Î¼Îµ Î±Î½Ï„Î¯ÏƒÏ„ÏÎ¿Ï†Î· ÏƒÎµÎ¹ÏÎ¬.<br/>-------------------------------------------------------<br/>"Î”ÎµÏÏ„ÎµÏÎ¿ ÎµÏ€Î¹Ï‡ÎµÎ¯ÏÎ·Î¼Î±"<br/>-------------------------------------------------------<br/>#Î ÏÏÏ„Î¿ ÎµÏ€Î¹Ï‡ÎµÎ¯ÏÎ·Î¼Î± #<br/>-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------<br/># Î”Î¹ÎµÏÎ¸Ï…Î½ÏƒÎ· ÎµÏ€Î¹ÏƒÏ„ÏÎ¿Ï†Î®Ï‚ #<br/>--------------- JSR R5, CSV<br/>ÎŸ Ï€Î±Î»Î¹ÏŒÏ‚ R5 value Î¿ Ï€Î±Î»Î¹ÏŒÏ‚ R5...<br/>-------------------------------------------------------<br/>Î ÏÎ¿Î·Î³Î¿Ï…Î¼ÎµÎ½Î¿ ÎµÏ€Î¹Ï‡ÏÎ¹ÏƒÎ¼Î±<br/># Î‘ÏÎ¹Î¸Î¼ÏŒÏ‚ # ÎœÎ¹Î± ÏƒÏ…Î½Î¬ÏÏ„Î·ÏƒÎ· Ï€Î¿Ï… Î»Î±Î¼Î²Î¬Î½ÎµÎ¹ Î¼ÏŒÎ½Î¿ Î¼Î¯Î± Î»Î­Î¾Î· Ï‰Ï‚ Ï€Î±ÏÎ¬Î¼ÎµÏ„ÏÎ¿ Î¼Ï€Î¿ÏÎµÎ¯ Î½Î± ÎºÎ»Î·Î¸ÎµÎ¯ Î±Ï€Î»Î¬ Î¼ÎµÏ„Î±ÎºÎ¹Î½ÏÎ½Ï„Î±Ï‚ Ï„Î·Î½ Ï€Î±ÏÎ¬Î¼ÎµÏ„ÏÎ¿ ÏƒÎµ (SP) ÎºÎ±Î¹ ÎºÎ±Î»ÏÎ½Ï„Î±Ï‚ Ï„Î· ÏƒÏ…Î½Î¬ÏÏ„Î·ÏƒÎ·, Ï‡Ï‰ÏÎ¯Ï‚ Î½Î± Ï‡ÏÎµÎ¹Î¬Î¶ÎµÏ„Î±Î¹ Î½Î± ÎºÎ±Î¸Î±ÏÎ¯ÏƒÎµÎ¹ Ï„Î·Î½ Ï€Î±ÏÎ¬Î¼ÎµÏ„ÏÎ¿ Î±Ï€ÏŒ Ï„Î· ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î± ÎºÎ±Ï„Î¬ Ï„Î·Î½ ÎµÏ€Î¹ÏƒÏ„ÏÎ¿Ï†Î®. ÎŸÏ€Î¿Î¹ÎµÏƒÎ´Î®Ï€Î¿Ï„Îµ Ï€Î±ÏÎ¬Î¼ÎµÏ„ÏÎ¿Î¹ Ï€ÎµÏÎ¬ÏƒÎ¿Ï…Î½ Î¼ÎµÏ„Î¬ Ï„Î·Î½ Ï€ÏÏÏ„Î· (ÏƒÏ„Î·Î½ Ï€ÏÎ±Î³Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÏŒÏ„Î·Ï„Î± "Nth") Ï€ÏÎ­Ï€ÎµÎ¹ Î½Î± Ï‰Î¸Î·Î¸Î¿ÏÎ½ Ï€ÏÎ¹Î½ Î±Ï€ÏŒ Ï„Î·Î½ ÎºÎ»Î®ÏƒÎ· ÎºÎ±Î¹ Î½Î± ÎºÎ±Î¸Î±ÏÎ¹ÏƒÏ„Î¿ÏÎ½ Î¼ÎµÏ„Î¬. Î‘Î½ Î· ÏƒÏ…Î½Î¬ÏÏ„Î·ÏƒÎ· Î´ÎµÎ½ Î­Ï‡ÎµÎ¹ Ï„Î¿Ï€Î¹ÎºÎ­Ï‚ Î¼ÎµÏ„Î±Î²Î»Î·Ï„Î­Ï‚ ÎºÎ±Î¹ Î´ÎµÎ½ ÎºÎ±Î»ÎµÎ¯ ÏƒÏ…Î½Î±ÏÏ„Î®ÏƒÎµÎ¹Ï‚, Î¸Î± ÎµÎºÏ‡Ï‰ÏÎ®ÏƒÎµÎ¹ ÎºÎ±Î¼Î¯Î± ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î± ÎºÎ±Î¹ Î· Î»Î­Î¾Î· Î¼Îµ Ï„Î·Î½ ÎµÏ„Î¹ÎºÎ­Ï„Î± Â«first local varÂ» Î¸Î± ÎµÎ¯Î½Î±Î¹ Î±Ï‡ÏÎ·ÏƒÎ¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î·Ï„Î·.<br/>Î•Î¯Î½Î±Î¹ ÏƒÎ·Î¼Î±Î½Ï„Î¹ÎºÏŒ Î½Î± ÏƒÎ·Î¼ÎµÎ¹Ï‰Î¸ÎµÎ¯ ÏŒÏ„Î¹ Î¿Î¹ ÏÎ¿Ï…Ï„Î¯Î½Î±Ï‚ Î³Î½Ï‰ÏÎ¯Î¶Î¿Ï…Î½ Ï€ÏŒÏƒÎ± Î¿ÏÎ¯ÏƒÎ¼Î±Ï„Î± Ï€ÎµÏÎ½Î¿ÏÎ½ ÏƒÎµ Î¼Î¹Î± ÏƒÏ…Î½Î¬ÏÏ„Î·ÏƒÎ·, ÎºÎ±Î¹ Î¸Î± Ï€ÏÎ¿ÏƒÎ±ÏÎ¼ÏŒÏƒÎ¿Ï…Î½ Ï„Î· ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î± Î±Î½Î¬Î»Î¿Î³Î± Î¼ÎµÏ„Î¬ Î±Ï€ÏŒ Î­Î½Î± func-<br/>Î•Ï€Î¹ÏƒÏ„ÏÎ­Ï†ÎµÎ¹ Î¿ Î¹ÏŒÏ‚.<br/>Î£Î—ÎœÎ•Î™Î©Î£Î—<br/>Î‘Ï…Ï„Î® Î· Î¼Î¿ÏÏ†Î® Ï€Î»Î±Î¹ÏƒÎ¯Î¿Ï… ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î±Ï‚ ÎµÎ¯Î½Î±Î¹ Î· Î¯Î´Î¹Î± Î¼Îµ Î±Ï…Ï„Î® Ï€Î¿Ï… Ï‡ÏÎ·ÏƒÎ¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¹ÎµÎ¯Ï„Î±Î¹ Î±Ï€ÏŒ ÎµÏ€Î¹ÎºÎ±Î»Ï…Ï€Ï„ÏŒÎ¼ÎµÎ½Î± Î±Î½Ï„Î¹ÎºÎµÎ¯Î¼ÎµÎ½Î± ÏƒÏ„Î¿ 2.9BSD.<br/>Î‘Î¡Î§Î—Î“ÎŸÎ£<br/>Î¤Î¶Î¿Î½ Î¦. Î“Î¿Ï…Î½Ï„Ï‚, MIT Concouse Computer Center<br/>3Î· Î´Î¹Î±Î½Î¿Î¼Î® ÎœÏ€Î­ÏÎºÎ»ÎµÏŠSTACK(5)<br/><br/>Check Out this Related Man Î£ÎµÎ»Î¯Î´Î±<br/><br/>STACK(9) Î•Î³Ï‡ÎµÎ¹ÏÎ¯Î´Î¹Î¿ Ï„Î¿Ï… BSD Kernel Developer STACK(9)NAME stack -- kernel thread stack tracing ruines<br/>Î£Î¥ÎÎŸÎ¨Î—<br/>#include #sys/param.h> (ÏƒÏ„Î± Î‘Î³Î³Î»Î¹ÎºÎ¬).<br/>#include #sys/stack.h> (ÏƒÏ„Î± Î‘Î³Î³Î»Î¹ÎºÎ¬).<br/>Î£Ï„Î¿ Î±ÏÏ‡ÎµÎ¯Î¿ ÏÏ…Î¸Î¼Î¯ÏƒÎµÏ‰Î½ Ï„Î¿Ï… Ï€Ï…ÏÎ®Î½Î±:<br/>Î•Ï€Î¹Î»Î¿Î³Î­Ï‚ DDB Î•Ï€Î¹Î»Î¿Î³Î­Ï‚ ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î±Ï‚ STACK struct *<br/>stack_create(void); void stack_destroy(struct stack *st); int stack_put(struct stack *st); vm_offset_t pc; void stack(src); void stack_zero(struct stack *st); void stack_print(st); void stack_bprint_short_short;<br/>Î Î•Î¡Î™Î“Î¡Î‘Î¦Î—<br/>Î— ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î± KPI ÎµÏ€Î¹Ï„ÏÎ­Ï€ÎµÎ¹ Ï„Î·Î½ Î±Î½Î±Î¶Î®Ï„Î·ÏƒÎ· Ï€Î»Î·ÏÎ¿Ï†Î¿ÏÎ¹ÏÎ½ Î±Î½Î¯Ï‡Î½ÎµÏ…ÏƒÎ·Ï‚ ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î±Ï‚ Ï€Ï…ÏÎ®Î½Î± ÎºÎ±Î¹ Ï„Î·Î½ Î±Ï…Ï„Î¿Î¼Î±Ï„Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¹Î·Î¼Î­Î½Î· Î´Î·Î¼Î¹Î¿Ï…ÏÎ³Î¯Î± ÏƒÏ…Î¼Î²Î¿Î»Î¿ÏƒÎµÎ¹ÏÏÎ½ Î±Î½Î¯Ï‡Î½ÎµÏ…ÏƒÎ·Ï‚ ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î±Ï‚ Ï€Ï…ÏÎ®Î½Î± Î³Î¹Î± Ï„Î¿Ï…Ï‚ ÏƒÎºÎ¿Ï€Î¿ÏÏ‚ Ï„Î·Ï‚ Î±Ï€Î¿ÏƒÏ†Î±Î»Î¼Î¬Ï„Ï‰ÏƒÎ·Ï‚ ÎºÎ±Î¹ ÎµÎ½Ï„Î¿Ï€Î¹ÏƒÎ¼Î¿Ï. Î“Î¹Î± Î½Î± Ï‡ÏÎ·ÏƒÎ¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¹Î®ÏƒÎµÏ„Îµ Ï„Î¿ KPI, Ï„Î¿Ï…Î»Î¬Ï‡Î¹ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î½ Î¼Î¯Î± Î±Ï€ÏŒ Ï„Î¹Ï‚ ÎµÏ€Î¹Î»Î¿Î³Î­Ï‚ DDB ÎºÎ±Î¹ ÎµÏ€Î¹Î»Î¿Î³Î­Ï‚ STACK Ï€ÏÎ­Ï€ÎµÎ¹ Î½Î± Î¼ÎµÏ„Î±Î³Î»Ï‰Ï„Ï„Î¹ÏƒÏ„ÎµÎ¯ ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î½ Ï€Ï…ÏÎ®Î½Î±.<br/>ÎšÎ¬Î¸Îµ Î¯Ï‡Î½Î¿Ï‚ ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î±Ï‚ Ï€ÎµÏÎ¹Î³ÏÎ¬Ï†ÎµÏ„Î±Î¹ Î±Ï€ÏŒ Î¼Î¹Î± ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î¯Î²Î± Î´Î¿Î¼Î¹ÎºÏÎ½ ÎºÎ±Ï„Î±ÏƒÎºÎµÏ…ÏÎ½. Î ÏÎ¹Î½ Î´Î·Î¼Î¹Î¿Ï…ÏÎ³Î·Î¸ÎµÎ¯ Î­Î½Î± Î¯Ï‡Î½Î¿Ï‚ Î® Ï‡ÎµÎ¹ÏÎ±Î³Ï‰Î³Î·Î¸ÎµÎ¯ Î¼Îµ Î¬Î»Î»Î¿ Ï„ÏÏŒÏ€Î¿, Î· Î±Ï€Î¿Î¸Î®ÎºÎµÏ…ÏƒÎ· Î³Î¹Î± Ï„Î¿ Î¯Ï‡Î½Î¿Ï‚ Ï€ÏÎ­Ï€ÎµÎ¹ Î½Î± ÎµÎ¯Î½Î±Î¹ allo-<br/>cated with stack_create(), Ï„Î¿ Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î¿ Î¼Ï€Î¿ÏÎµÎ¯ Î½Î± ÎºÎ¿Î¹Î¼Î·Î¸ÎµÎ¯. | The best way to Develop Tomatoes in Your Backyard<br/><br/>The best way to Develop Tomatoes in Your Backyard<br/>by The Editorial Group<br/><br/>Tomatoes are a gardening favourite. Their plump purple or yellow fruit have truly found their technique into the cooking space and into a spread of dishes. They're utilized in salads, stews, soups, and sauces. Tomatoes will be canned or sun-dried. Tomatoes are a heat climate situation crop. They require plenty of sunshine and fertile soil to provide and set up at their best. Tomato seeds and seedlings or "slips" are available in plenty of ranges.<br/>Regardless of which vary you choose, it's vital to start by conditioning the soil the place you put together to develop your crop.<br/><br/>Tomatoes like ample, well-drained soil so begin by mixing ample uncooked materials into the soil. You may make the most of a mixture of backyard compost and dried manure to lighten the soil and provide a steady provide of vitamins.<br/>Until the soil and blend to a depth of about 8 inches. This may permit the roots of the crops to broaden and set up accurately.<br/>You will get the seed packages out of your regional backyard store or by means of mail order in case you imply to start your crops from seeds.<br/>The good thing about starting tomatoes from seeds is that you should have a broader vary from which to pick out. Plant seeds a half inch deep in little pots together with an ample, moist potting soil combine.<br/>Cowl seeds with a half inch of soil. Tomato seedlings or "slips" are available from the regional backyard store, usually in early spring. Seedlings are significantly better match for areas the place the climate situation is cooler in spring.<br/>When they're about 6 inches excessive and the outside soil temperature stage is no less than fifty levels Fahrenheit, transplant seedlings outside.<br/>Tomatoes require nice offers of sunshine. When the situations are perfect for transplanting, plant seedlings 3 inches deep in a gap with adequate area for the roots. Cowl the roots with soil and water gently.<br/><br/>Tomato crops can mature to three ft highâ€“ relying upon the rangeâ€“ and require to be supported. Location a wire cage across the crops merely after transplanting or embrace wooden stakes beside the crops.<br/>Because the crops develop, weave the limbs by means of the wire cage in order that the fruit will develop exterior the cage. With stakes, merely loop a string across the crops and shield.<br/>Embody mulch across the crops with straw to take care of water. Maintain the soil moist across the crops nevertheless don't over water. When they're the popular dimension, collect the tomatoes. When they're primarily inexperienced nevertheless agency and easily starting to ripen, you'll be able to allow the tomatoes to ripen on the plant or you'll be able to collect them.<br/>Fried inexperienced tomatoes are a Southern favourite. You may make the most of the tomatoes contemporary off the plant; peel and save them in your freezer, or dry them for in a while utilization. Tomatoes are the first lively ingredient in plenty of dishes similar to tomato sauce for meatloaf and spaghetti.<br/>Tomatoes are excessive in Vitamin A, Vitamin Potassium, c and iron. Nutrient-rich tomatoes likewise include thiamin, phosphorus, and calcium. Tomatoes are delicious, easy and wholesome to develop. | When do you take Ganirelix during IVF?<br/><br/>Ganirelix or Cetrotide are usually started on (about) the sixth day of giving the FSH product that stimulates the development of follicles in the ovary. They are commonly given subcutaneously once daily and continued until HCG is given.<br/><br/>What day of cycle is IVF retrieval?<br/><br/>Egg Retrieval Process & Timelines The egg retrieval process is most often put in motion by the start of stimulation medications for an IVF or Egg Freezing treatment. These medications are usually started on days 2-4 of a woman's natural menstrual cycle and taken for approximately ten days.<br/><br/>What does Ganirelix do in IVF?<br/><br/>Ganirelix is usually used in combination with other hormones (FSH and hCG). It works by blocking the release of a certain hormone (luteinizing hormone). Ganirelix stops eggs from being released too early and gives the eggs time to grow properly.<br/><br/>How long did you Stim before egg retrieval?<br/><br/>The stimulation phase involves the injection of medications for 8-14 days, to induce the ovaries to produce many eggs.<br/><br/>When do you start Ganirelix?<br/><br/>You will be instructed to start Ganirelix AcetateÂ® or CetrotideÂ® after you start gonadotropins, when your largest follicles are larger than 12 millimeters.<br/><br/>Do follicles continue to grow after trigger shot?<br/><br/>In general, in order to achieve maturity, we will wait until the leading follicles are at least 18 mms. If the follicle does not reach 18-20 mms, it is unlikely that the follicle will ovulate despite HCG (Ovidrel). They do continue to grow a little, but the follicle has not reached ovulatory size.<br/><br/>Is 6 eggs enough for IVF?<br/><br/>This is why IVF centers stimulate women in order to get sufficient eggs. Women under 38 in our IVF program have acceptable live birth rates even with only 3 â€“ 6 eggs, do better with more than 6 eggs, and do best with more than 10 eggs.<br/><br/>What percentage of fertilized eggs make it to Day 5?<br/><br/>Remember, even if all of your embryos are perfect on day 3, on average only 40-50% of them will become blastocyst on day 5.<br/><br/>Is 2 eggs good for IVF?<br/><br/>An average of ten to 20 eggs are usually retrieved for IVF, but the number can be higher or lower. You would think more eggs is always better, but that's not the case. Researchers who analyzed thousands of IVF cycles found that the magic number of eggs that lead to a live birth is 15.<br/><br/>Which is better cetrotide or Ganirelix?<br/><br/>Cetrotide (cetrorelix) is a fertility treatment that you can give to yourself at home, but it is expensive. A protocol that uses Antagon (Ganirelix) will be shorter and will have overall less injections than other options.<br/><br/>How many follicles are good for IVF?<br/><br/>Follicles Needed for an IVF Cycle During IVF treatment, your doctor wants to stimulate your ovaries to mature several follicles. Anywhere between 8 and 15 follicles is considered an acceptable amount.<br/><br/>When do you trigger for IVF?<br/><br/>Ovulation Induction: Between Day 8 and 12 Ovulation is triggered with an injection of human chorionic gonadotropin (HCG), lupron, or both. Trigger is administered when the follicles are judged to be mature, usually 8 and 12 days after the start of injectable fertility medications.<br/><br/>What happens if you ovulate before egg retrieval?<br/><br/>Mistimed hCG/trigger Shot If it's taken at the wrong time, the eggs may ovulate before your procedure. Once the eggs are released into the pelvic cavity, they can't be retrieved for IVF. Your doctor will give you an exact time to give yourself this injection. | Î ÏŒÏ„Îµ Ï€Î±Î¯ÏÎ½ÎµÏ„Îµ Ï„Î¿ Ganirelix ÎºÎ±Ï„Î¬ Ï„Î· Î´Î¹Î¬ÏÎºÎµÎ¹Î± Ï„Î·Ï‚ ÎµÎ¾Ï‰ÏƒÏ‰Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÎ®Ï‚ Î³Î¿Î½Î¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î·ÏƒÎ·Ï‚;<br/><br/>Î¤Î¿ Ganirelix Î® Ï„Î¿ Cetrotide ÏƒÏ…Î½Î®Î¸Ï‰Ï‚ Î¾ÎµÎºÎ¹Î½Î¿ÏÎ½ (Ï€ÎµÏÎ¯Ï€Î¿Ï…) Ï„Î·Î½ Î­ÎºÏ„Î· Î·Î¼Î­ÏÎ± Î±Ï€ÏŒ Ï„Î· Ï‡Î¿ÏÎ®Î³Î·ÏƒÎ· Ï„Î¿Ï… Ï€ÏÎ¿ÏŠÏŒÎ½Ï„Î¿Ï‚ FSH Ï€Î¿Ï… Î´Î¹ÎµÎ³ÎµÎ¯ÏÎµÎ¹ Ï„Î·Î½ Î±Î½Î¬Ï€Ï„Ï…Î¾Î· Ï„Ï‰Î½ Ï‰Î¿Î¸Ï…Î»Î±ÎºÎ¯Ï‰Î½ ÏƒÏ„Î·Î½ Ï‰Î¿Î¸Î®ÎºÎ·. ÎˆÎ½Î± Ï€ÏÏ‰Ï„ÏŒÎºÎ¿Î»Î»Î¿ Ï€Î¿Ï… Ï‡ÏÎ·ÏƒÎ¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¹ÎµÎ¯ Ï„Î¿ Antagon (Ganirelix) Î¸Î± ÎµÎ¯Î½Î±Î¹ Î¼Î¹ÎºÏÏŒÏ„ÎµÏÎ¿ ÎºÎ±Î¹ Î¸Î± Î­Ï‡ÎµÎ¹ ÏƒÏ…Î½Î¿Î»Î¹ÎºÎ¬ Î»Î¹Î³ÏŒÏ„ÎµÏÎµÏ‚ ÎµÎ½Î­ÏƒÎµÎ¹Ï‚ Î±Ï€ÏŒ Î¬Î»Î»ÎµÏ‚ ÎµÏ€Î¹Î»Î¿Î³Î­Ï‚.<br/><br/>Î ÏŒÏƒÎ± Ï‰Î¿Î¸Ï…Î»Î¬ÎºÎ¹Î± ÎµÎ¯Î½Î±Î¹ ÎºÎ±Î»Î¬ Î³Î¹Î± ÎµÎ¾Ï‰ÏƒÏ‰Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÎ® Î³Î¿Î½Î¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î·ÏƒÎ·;<br/><br/>ÎŸÎ¹ Ï‰Î¿Î¸Î®ÎºÎµÏ‚ Ï‡ÏÎµÎ¹Î¬Î¶Î¿Î½Ï„Î±Î¹ Î³Î¹Î± Î­Î½Î±Î½ ÎºÏÎºÎ»Î¿ ÎµÎ¾Ï‰ÏƒÏ‰Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÎ®Ï‚ Î³Î¿Î½Î¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î·ÏƒÎ·Ï‚ ÎšÎ±Ï„Î¬ Ï„Î· Î´Î¹Î¬ÏÎºÎµÎ¹Î± Ï„Î·Ï‚ Î¸ÎµÏÎ±Ï€ÎµÎ¯Î±Ï‚ Î¼Îµ ÎµÎ¾Ï‰ÏƒÏ‰Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÎ® Î³Î¿Î½Î¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î·ÏƒÎ·, Î¿ Î³Î¹Î±Ï„ÏÏŒÏ‚ ÏƒÎ±Ï‚ Î¸Î­Î»ÎµÎ¹ Î½Î± Î´Î¹ÎµÎ³ÎµÎ¯ÏÎµÎ¹ Ï„Î¹Ï‚ Ï‰Î¿Î¸Î®ÎºÎµÏ‚ ÏƒÎ±Ï‚ Î³Î¹Î± Î½Î± Ï‰ÏÎ¹Î¼Î¬ÏƒÎµÎ¹ Î±ÏÎºÎµÏ„Î¬ Ï‰Î¿Î¸Ï…Î»Î¬ÎºÎ¹Î±. ÎŸÏ€Î¿Ï…Î´Î®Ï€Î¿Ï„Îµ Î¼ÎµÏ„Î±Î¾Ï 8 ÎºÎ±Î¹ 15 Ï‰Î¿Î¸Ï…Î»Î±ÎºÎ¯Ï‰Î½ Î¸ÎµÏ‰ÏÎµÎ¯Ï„Î±Î¹ Î±Ï€Î¿Î´ÎµÎºÏ„Î® Ï€Î¿ÏƒÏŒÏ„Î·Ï„Î±.<br/><br/>Î ÏŒÏ„Îµ ÎµÎ½ÎµÏÎ³Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¹ÎµÎ¯Ï‚ Ï„Î·Î½ ÎµÎ¾Ï‰ÏƒÏ‰Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÎ® Î³Î¿Î½Î¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î·ÏƒÎ·;<br/><br/>Î•Ï€Î±Î³Ï‰Î³Î® Ï‰Î¿ÏÏÎ·Î¾Î¯Î±Ï‚: ÎœÎµÏ„Î±Î¾Ï Ï„Î·Ï‚ Î—Î¼Î­ÏÎ±Ï‚ 8 ÎºÎ±Î¹ 12 Î— Ï‰Î¿ÏÏÎ·Î¾Î¯Î± Ï€Ï…ÏÎ¿Î´Î¿Ï„ÎµÎ¯Ï„Î±Î¹ Î¼Îµ Î­Î½ÎµÏƒÎ· Î±Î½Î¸ÏÏÏ€Î¹Î½Î·Ï‚ Ï‡Î¿ÏÎ¹Î±ÎºÎ®Ï‚ Î³Î¿Î½Î±Î´Î¿Ï„ÏÎ¿Ï€Î¯Î½Î·Ï‚ (HCG), Î»Î¿ÏÏ€ÏÎ¿Ï…, Î® ÎºÎ±Î¹ Ï„Î± Î´ÏÎ¿. Î— Î´Î¹Î­Î³ÎµÏÏƒÎ· Ï‡Î¿ÏÎ·Î³ÎµÎ¯Ï„Î±Î¹ ÏŒÏ„Î±Î½ Ï„Î± Ï‰Î¿Î¸Ï…Î»Î¬ÎºÎ¹Î± ÎºÏÎ¹Î¸Î¿ÏÎ½ ÏÏÎ¹Î¼Î±, ÏƒÏ…Î½Î®Î¸Ï‰Ï‚ 8 ÎºÎ±Î¹ 12 Î·Î¼Î­ÏÎµÏ‚ Î¼ÎµÏ„Î¬ Ï„Î·Î½ Î­Î½Î±ÏÎ¾Î· Ï„Ï‰Î½ ÎµÎ½Î­ÏƒÎ¹Î¼Ï‰Î½ Ï†Î±ÏÎ¼Î¬ÎºÏ‰Î½ Î³Î¿Î½Î¹Î¼ÏŒÏ„Î·Ï„Î±Ï‚.<br/><br/>Î¤Î¹ Î¸Î± ÏƒÏ…Î¼Î²ÎµÎ¯ Î±Î½ Î­Ï‡ÎµÏ„Îµ Ï‰Î¿ÏÏÎ·Î¾Î¯Î± Ï€ÏÎ¹Î½ Ï„Î·Î½ Ï‰Î¿Î»Î·ÏˆÎ¯Î±;<br/><br/>Î›Î±Î½Î¸Î±ÏƒÎ¼Î­Î½Î¿ hCG/trigger Shot Î‘Î½ Î»Î·Ï†Î¸ÎµÎ¯ ÏƒÎµ Î»Î¬Î¸Î¿Ï‚ ÏƒÏ„Î¹Î³Î¼Î®, Ï„Î± Î±Ï…Î³Î¬ Î¼Ï€Î¿ÏÎµÎ¯ Î½Î± Ï‰Î¿ÏÏÎ·Î¾Î¯Î± Ï€ÏÎ¹Î½ Î±Ï€ÏŒ Ï„Î· Î´Î¹Î±Î´Î¹ÎºÎ±ÏƒÎ¯Î± ÏƒÎ±Ï‚. ÎœÏŒÎ»Î¹Ï‚ Ï„Î± Î±Ï…Î³Î¬ Î±Ï€ÎµÎ»ÎµÏ…Î¸ÎµÏÏÎ½Î¿Î½Ï„Î±Î¹ ÏƒÏ„Î·Î½ Ï€Ï…ÎµÎ»Î¹ÎºÎ® ÎºÎ¿Î¹Î»ÏŒÏ„Î·Ï„Î±, Î´ÎµÎ½ Î¼Ï€Î¿ÏÎ¿ÏÎ½ Î½Î± Î±Î½Î±ÎºÏ„Î·Î¸Î¿ÏÎ½ Î³Î¹Î± ÎµÎ¾Ï‰ÏƒÏ‰Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÎ® Î³Î¿Î½Î¹Î¼Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¯Î·ÏƒÎ·. ÎŸ Î³Î¹Î±Ï„ÏÏŒÏ‚ ÏƒÎ±Ï‚ Î¸Î± ÏƒÎ±Ï‚ Î´ÏÏƒÎµÎ¹ Î±ÎºÏÎ¹Î²Î® Ï‡ÏÏŒÎ½Î¿ Î³Î¹Î± Î½Î± ÎºÎ¬Î½ÎµÏ„Îµ ÏƒÏ„Î¿Î½ ÎµÎ±Ï…Ï„ÏŒ ÏƒÎ±Ï‚ Î±Ï…Ï„Î® Ï„Î·Î½ Î­Î½ÎµÏƒÎ·. |
| I'm honoured to have Gillian Mawson as a guest blogger on historywithatwist. Gillian's books are important works of social history that will be invaluable to anyone who wants to understand the impact of the World War II on the children of the time.<br/><br/>Gillian, a history researcher, has collected stories from 100 people who spent the war years as evacuees in England, Northern Ireland, Scotland and Wales. The stories are accompanied by family photographs. She included stories from Northern Ireland because they do not tend to receive as much attention as stories from the UK.<br/><br/>Gillian Mawson<br/><br/>Gillian has been collecting evacuation stories since 2008 when she interviewed 200 evacuees for her first book, 'Guernsey Evacuees; The Forgotten Evacuees of the Second World War'. Seventeen thousand people fled Guernsey to England in 1940, just before Germany occupied the Channel Islands.<br/><br/>Sadly, many of the people she interviewed have since died. Gillian runs a community group for evacuees in Manchester so they can share their stories with the community. She feels it is vital that the memories of evacuees are recorded and shared now before they are lost for ever.<br/><br/>On 1 September 1939, millions of British children were evacuated with their schools, but there were further waves of evacuation during the war years. The children were accompanied on their journeys by their teachers and sometimes by mothers, and Gillian's book includes stories from these adults.<br/><br/>Some children stated that they went to school one morning and were evacuated within a few hours, without having had the chance to say 'goodbye' to their parents. When their children did not return home at the usual time, mothers gathered at the school where they found short, stark notices pinned to the school gates. Over the next few days they would receive a postcard such as this, showing their new address.<br/><br/>One child's message home â€“ 'I Have Gone'. (Courtesy of the Emmanuel School at War archive)<br/><br/>However, these postcards had tragic consequences for one little boy. The young evacuee posted a card home from his new billet, then went for a walk, but in the unfamiliar surroundings, he somehow fell into the canal, where he drowned. His family were advised of his death that evening, but the next morning his postcard arrived with its cheerful inscription, 'Dear Mum & Dad, I am very happy here, don't worry about me.'<br/><br/>Gerry Mullan was six years old when he was evacuated from Belfast to County Tyrone in 1941.<br/><br/>'We went to Fintona, where we had lived three or four years earlier. I felt excited and apprehensive, because I wasn't sure what it was going to be like to live in someone else's house. My brother Joe and I<br/>were looked after by a woman called Mrs Martin, an old friend of my mother. She was good, but very strict. Mother came with us, but she and my younger brothers were housed four or five miles away.<br/><br/>We saw her once a week but it was a bit heart-rending. I renewed acquaintances with some of the children I had known years earlier, which was good, but although Mrs Martin was very kind I remember never being really sure whether I was happy or not. We<br/>were very hard-up in Tyrone, I remember the jotter I used at school had to be used in every margin, covers, everywhere I could get a scribble I filled it.<br/><br/>Gerry Mullan on the right, as a baby<br/><br/>My uncle came to see us once or twice a week and gave us money for a new school book, but of course the money went on ice-cream! We only lasted four months and came back to Belfast in July. It was sad in the end to leave because I was seven by then and beginning to enjoy it, as I had made a lot of friends. But it was great to get home and see my father again and be with mother full time.'<br/><br/>William Crawford was 11 years old when he was evacuated from Belfast to Portrush in 1942.<br/><br/>'I attended Cabin Hill School, Belfast, and one day I turned on the wireless to hear news of the declaration of war. I was horrified because my father was working in Ceylon so my parents might not be able to return until the end of Dad's contract. I experienced two air raids at school and on one occasion our Headmaster, 'Fluffy' Sutton, read Sherlock Holmes stories to us in the shelters.<br/><br/>There was no latrine, so we were allowed out for a pee, although sometimes we used to pretend, and stay out just a bit too long to watch the bombs and the fires of Belfast. In 1942 our school moved to the safety of Portrush where we were accommodated in hotels and boarding houses. One morning in 1945, I was told to travel to my Uncle Hubert's house in Belfast to meet my parents who I had not seen for over 7 years.<br/><br/>I entered the living room and saw two people, a man and a woman. The woman, my mother, asked, "Are you William?" I just nodded through teary eyes. Then Mother said to the man, "Matthew, are you going to say hello to William?" Matthew turned towards me and said "Are you my son?" My father and I shook hands. I didn't want to let go.'<br/><br/>William Crawford (right) cycling with his sisters Jean (left) and Alison (centre) in 1941. A year later William was evacuated to Portrush.<br/><br/>Gillian's book shows that many evacuees came to love their 'foster parents' and stayed in touch with them after the war. Some evacuees, however, were less well treated and a chapter of Gillian's book is devoted to their memories.<br/><br/>Every evacuee's story is different and this book, with its combination of 100 stories and family photographs, paints an intimate picture of the different ways in which the British people opened up their homes to evacuees.<br/><br/>'Evacuees: Children's Lives on the WW2 Home Front' by Gillian Mawson is published by Pen & SwordMy father was an evacuee. He lived on a farm from aged 6, for three years. One day two women asked him the way to the farm, he guided them and went on to post his letter home. When he got back to the farm the two women were sitting there drinking tea. They were introduced to him as his mother and eldest sister. I found it quite sad that a young child was torn from his mother, forgot her, and then was torn from another life back to a virtual stranger. He never left his mother's side after that, and was a loyal son. As one of ten children he nurtured his family until death parted them, a couple returned home with 'issues'. He took us to the farm when we were children, and the lady sobbed. It was an emotional day. He passed away two years ago, and I decided to look up the farm but sadly it has been destroyed. Glad he never knew.<br/><br/>Very poignant story, Glynis. It had never occurred to me that evacuees would be torn twice â€“ once from their parents and a second time from the foster parent. It must have made the whole experience doubly distressing.<br/><br/>This sounds like a must read. Northern Ireland also took in more than its fair share of Jewish child evacuees who came out of Germany and Austrian with the Kindertransport initiative immediately before the outbreak of war. Sadly, some of them were killed in the Belfast Blitz and many of them, when old enough, joined up and went back to fight the Nazis. Most lost their parents in the Holocaust and stayed on in Ireland. As Jewish adults, those who remained in the province were not allowed to join the local golf clubs, so they founded their own Jewish Golfing Society. However, Sir Otto Jaffe MP, himself the son of German Jewish migrants, became Mayor of Belfast, not once but twice.<br/><br/>As usual, Denise, you are a font of information. It's terrible to think of the children dying in the Blitz after all they had already gone through. â€“ and then the prejudice they encountered later as wellâ€¦<br/><br/>Hello History with a Twist. I am one of Gills Evacuees mentioned in her book. I always felt so sad for some of the evacuees who were ill treated at times, because I was one of the lucky ones, billeted with a lovely family and I did not want to go back home to living in Birmingham town at the end of the war. Not only because I was happy with the people but because I was in the country. Gills books are superbly written and she has brought many of the evacuees together again. Her books are our History.<br/><br/>Well said, Rita. I'm glad your evacuee experience was a positive one. It's very good of you to recognise the work Gill has done. Anyone who can bring people together in ways that she has, deserves great credit. Gill's books are a very important contribution to the social history of these isles. Thanks for dropping by. â€“ David | Î•Î¯Î½Î±Î¹ Ï„Î¹Î¼Î® Î¼Î¿Ï… Î½Î± Î­Ï‡Ï‰ Ï„Î·Î½ Î¤Î¶Î¯Î»Î¹Î±Î½ ÎœÎ¬Î¿Ï…ÏƒÎ¿Î½ Ï‰Ï‚ guest blogger ÏƒÏ„Î¿ historywithatwist. So when we start at great distances where the atoms are too far apart to really form a bond, we have an energy approaching zero. So we can start by drawing a diagram at high distance with energy approaching zero. And then as we get closer together, the energy will begin to decrease as the bond is forming until it reaches a minimum. And at that minimum is where we have the associated bond length of the cl to bond. As we continue to move to smaller and smaller distances, the energy will quickly increase as now the atoms when they get too close, begin to repel each other rather than form a bond. So here's a general potential energy diagram of a seal to bond. We note that the bond distance of 194 Pekka meters occurs right at the minimum point of this potential energy diagram. Additionally, the dissociation energy can be found by measuring the difference between the energy minimum and the energy of dissociation where the bond no longer exists. So when we measure this difference in energy, we can calculate it to be 240 killed joules per mole.<br/><br/>Answers #4<br/><br/>Hi friends here it is. Given the reduced months off. | Experts warn 'life of the mother' exceptions for abortion could still punish women, doctors<br/><br/>The bill lawmakers are expected to pass would allow abortions to prevent substantial permanent impairment of the life or physical health of the pregnant woman.<br/><br/>Credit: WTHR<br/><br/>Author: Rachael Krause<br/><br/>Published: 12:13 AM EDT August 5, 2022<br/><br/>Updated: 12:28 AM EDT August 5, 2022<br/><br/>INDIANAPOLIS â€” Indiana lawmakers are moving quickly through the special session, expected to ban abortions in the state with few exceptions.<br/><br/>One exception that's continued through the Senate and, so far, in the House, would be to allow abortions when a doctor is acting to save the life of the mother. But doctors and legal experts are warning that kind of language is vague, and these critical healthcare decisions need to be made without fear they could be criminalized for saving a pregnant person's life.<br/><br/>"It's really disappointing and it's scary for patients and for providers," said Dr. Caroline Rouse, a maternal fetal medicine physician at IU Health.<br/><br/>Rouse has been closely watching this special session, following lawmakers' plans closely as they work quickly to ban abortions in the Hoosier State. She said the decisions being made in the Statehouse to ban abortion may directly impact the kind of lifesaving care she's able to legally offer her patients.<br/><br/>"This is not black and white. There is no line before which something is only threatening to the health and not the life," Rouse said. "My job is to predict and prevent health complications and death as best I can and I'd rather do that as opposed to just waiting until there's a catastrophe and then intervening. That goes against everything that I've trained for and studied for."<br/><br/>The bill lawmakers are expected to pass would allow abortions to prevent substantial permanent impairment of the life or physical health of the pregnant woman. But Rouse said that's not as clear as lawmakers imagine it to be.<br/><br/>If a doctor acts in their best medical judgment to save a patient's life through an abortion, she said many physicians now worry that if others view that same situation as non-life-threatening, physicians could face criminal penalties or even jail time.<br/><br/>"There's a lot of concern about needing to call a lawyer before making a medical decision for someone who is sick and potentially very, very sick," Rouse said. "While we make every medical decision using the best medical knowledge and literature and experience we have, sometimes those decisions are fast and we don't have time to make medical decisions by committee and calling a lawyer and doing all these other things. So we're worried about it."<br/><br/>IU law professor Jennifer Drobac said challenging in the courts to ensure a woman can legally have an abortion would take time - time many women won't have when it comes to making a decision.<br/><br/>"You need to have this procedure right away if you've discovered there's a problem or there's a pregnancy and you don't want to wait. And court cases can take months and years to percolate through for decisions," Drobac said. "Suing after the fact may not deal with all the problems that have been created because you couldn't get a decision in the first instance. So again, there's a no-win outcome here."<br/><br/>Women forced to wait while a decision comes through the court system, Drobac said, could mean a woman dies from a healthcare complication or is forced to have the child anyway.<br/><br/>If a doctor does act to save a woman's life by providing an abortion, Drobac said under this proposed bill, what happens to the woman and doctor legally could come down to what judge or prosecutor you face and their own politics.<br/><br/>"Some judges may be very lenient and say, 'Yeah, close enough.' Some judges may not be lenient at all and say, 'No, you weren't close enough to death at all. You shouldn't have had this abortion.' And the prosecutor may go ahead and prosecute the doctor with criminal charges," Drobac said. | ÎŸÎ¹ ÎµÎ¹Î´Î¹ÎºÎ¿Î¯ Ï€ÏÎ¿ÎµÎ¹Î´Î¿Ï€Î¿Î¹Î¿ÏÎ½ ÏŒÏ„Î¹ Î¿Î¹ ÎµÎ¾Î±Î¹ÏÎ­ÏƒÎµÎ¹Ï‚ Â«Î¶Ï‰Î®Ï‚ Ï„Î·Ï‚ Î¼Î·Ï„Î­ÏÎ±Ï‚Â» Î³Î¹Î± Ï„Î¹Ï‚ Î±Î¼Î²Î»ÏÏƒÎµÎ¹Ï‚ Î¸Î± Î¼Ï€Î¿ÏÎ¿ÏÏƒÎ±Î½ Î±ÎºÏŒÎ¼Î± Î½Î± Ï„Î¹Î¼Ï‰ÏÎ®ÏƒÎ¿Ï…Î½ Ï„Î¹Ï‚ Î³Ï…Î½Î±Î¯ÎºÎµÏ‚, Ï„Î¿Ï…Ï‚ Î³Î¹Î±Ï„ÏÎ¿ÏÏ‚<br/><br/>Î¤Î¿ Î½Î¿Î¼Î¿ÏƒÏ‡Î­Î´Î¹Î¿ Ï€Î¿Ï… Î±Î½Î±Î¼Î­Î½ÎµÏ„Î±Î¹ Î½Î± Ï€ÎµÏÎ¬ÏƒÎ¿Ï…Î½ Î¿Î¹ Î½Î¿Î¼Î¿Î¸Î­Ï„ÎµÏ‚ Î¸Î± ÎµÏ€Î­Ï„ÏÎµÏ€Îµ ÏƒÏ„Î¹Ï‚ Î±Î¼Î²Î»ÏÏƒÎµÎ¹Ï‚ Î½Î± Î±Ï€Î¿Ï„ÏÎ­ÏˆÎ¿Ï…Î½ Î¿Ï…ÏƒÎ¹Î±ÏƒÏ„Î¹ÎºÎ® Î¼ÏŒÎ½Î¹Î¼Î· Î²Î»Î¬Î²Î· Ï„Î·Ï‚ Î¶Ï‰Î®Ï‚ Î® Ï„Î·Ï‚ ÏƒÏ‰Î¼Î±Ï„Î¹ÎºÎ®Ï‚ Ï…Î³ÎµÎ¯Î±Ï‚ Ï„Î·Ï‚ ÎµÎ³ÎºÏÎ¿Ï….<br/><br/>Î Î¯ÏƒÏ„Ï‰ÏƒÎ·: WTHR<br/><br/>Î£Ï…Î³Î³ÏÎ±Ï†Î­Î±Ï‚: Rachael Krause<br/><br/>Î”Î·Î¼Î¿ÏƒÎ¹ÎµÏÎ¸Î·ÎºÎµ: 12:13 Ï€.Î¼.
